- Term 2: `A^2/(c*A^4 + 1)` — a rational function

What about `A*k/(A^2 + d)`? This gives `kA/(A^2+d)`. For this to equal `A^2/(cA^4+1)`, we'd need `kA(cA^4+1) = A^2(A^2+d)`, i.e., `kcA^5 + kA = A^4 + dA^2`. This doesn't work — different powers.

Let me check candidates with `A*c1/(A*c2+1)^2`:
`A/(A*c+1)^2 = A/(c^2*A^2 + 2cA + 1)`. This is `A/(quadratic in A)`, while GT needs `A^2/(quartic in A)`. Not equivalent.

What about combining `A^2*c0 + A^2*c1/(A^2+c2)^2`? This gives `A^2[c0(A^2+c2)^2 + c1]/(A^2+c2)^2`. The denominator is `A^4 + 2c2*A^2 + c2^2`. GT denominator is `cA^4 + 1`. For matching: `2c2 = 0` → `c2 = 0`, but then denominator is `A^4`, losing the constant. Doesn't work.

What about `A^2*c0 + A^2*c1/(A^2+c2)`? Combined: `A^2[c0(A^2+c2)+c1]/(A^2+c2) = A^2(c0*A^2 + c0*c2 + c1)/(A^2+c2)`. GT is `A^2(c0*cA^4 + c0 + c1)/(cA^4+1)`. Denominator degree doesn't match.
